# Data Planning Strategy And Compliance For Ai Initiatives

> Dive into AI strategies that propel organizational goals with expert guidance from cloud architect, author, and Google Cloud expert Dan Sullivan. Learn how to align AI technologies with business objectives. Discover best practices for sourcing data, ensuring data quality, and preserving privacy. Gain insights into structured, semi-structured, and unstructured data, through topics such as batch and

### 1. Data Collection Fundamentals

#### Identifying data sources
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's consider how we go about identifying data sources.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=4)** Now in this section, we're going to explore various internal, external, and synthetic data sources that we can use to power our AI initiatives.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=13)** We'll also consider key factors to evaluate potential data sources against our specific business needs.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=20)** We're also going to consider how to navigate legal and ethical landscapes when sourcing data and understand the common pitfalls and red flags when evaluating potential data sources.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=32)** Now with regards to internal data sources, we have things like department databases and data warehouses, which are our existing repositories that contain structured information that's already aligned with business processes.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=45)** And we also have enterprise-scale systems like CRMs and ERPs, which hold rich customer and operational data.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=53)** And we want to be careful not to overlook employee-generated documents and other content because they contain valuable institutional knowledge and expertise that can be leveraged by AI.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=65)** Now with regards to external data sources, there are multiple types, including public datasets from government, academic, and open data initiatives, commercial datasets from vendors that offer specialized datasets.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=80)** But we do want to be careful to evaluate licensing costs and terms when working with commercial providers.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=86)** Similarly, there are service providers that offer APIs, and the APIs provide real-time access to third party data with standardized formats.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=96)** Web scraping is really useful for gathering publicly available information.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=101)** We also want to keep in mind social media and public forums.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=104)** Now these sources provide insight into customer sentiment and trends and related kinds of information.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=111)** Now, sometimes we have to turn to synthetic datasets.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=114)** For example, we use synthetic datasets when we have privacy concerns because synthetic datasets offer solutions when privacy regulations restrict the use of real customer information.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=126)** We also use augmented datasets.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=129)** Now this is a hybrid approach that combine actual data with synthetic elements to help address gaps or enhance features.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=136)** And we can also use AI to create diverse training examples for scenarios that are difficult to collect naturally, and that's especially true for edge cases.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=145)** Now we want to think in terms of relevance and alignment, that data sources must align with our AI initiative that we're trying to accomplish.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=153)** We also want to ensure that the data reflects our specific industry realities and application scenarios.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=160)** And we want to verify the data includes the variables that our models will need to make accurate predictions.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=167)** We also want to consider data quality factors such as completeness, and we do that by evaluating whether the data has all the necessary fields.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=178)** We also want to think about accuracy in terms of verifying the information is correct and reasonably free of errors.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=185)** With regards to consistency, we want to check if the data is formatted uniformly across sources.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=192)** Data should also be timely.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=194)** That means we need to assess if the data is current enough for our specific application needs.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=199)** We also want to determine if the level of detail is sufficient without being unnecessarily complex.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=205)** There are several technical considerations to keep in mind when identifying data sources.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=211)** We want to evaluate how difficult it will be to incorporate data into our existing workflows and systems.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=219)** We also want to ensure that data formats work with our chosen AI platforms to minimize conversion efforts.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=226)** Also, we want to assess whether we have the infrastructure needed to handle the data volume, the velocity, and the complexity of the data we're considering.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=235)** We also want to consider how often the data needs refreshing and the resources required to keep it current.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=242)** We also need to consider legal requirements around our data sources.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=247)** Particularly, we want to verify that we have the proper rights to use the data for our intended AI applications.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=254)** We also want to ensure adherence to frameworks like GDPR and California Consumer Privacy Acts, and other privacy laws affecting our operations.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=265)** We should identify and address any industry-specific regulatory requirements that are unique to our sector.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=270)** So for example, HIPAA in healthcare, or FCRA for financial services.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=277)** We also want to be careful when we navigate the complex landscape of international data movement, and this is particularly important for organizations that operate on a global scale.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=288)** With regards to risk management, we want to establish processes to validate the origin and chain of custody of all of our data sources.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=297)** We also want to evaluate how well providers protect their data, especially for sensitive information.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=302)** We also need to understand the track record of the companies that we are dealing with.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=309)** And we want to consider potential dependencies and plan for alternatives if we need to swap providers.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=316)** Now, there are some things we want to watch out for, such as gaps or outdated information because that can often indicate deeper quality issues that can undermine the quality of our AI models.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=327)** Without understanding how data's collected, we can't properly assess its suitability, so we need adequate documentation.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=335)** We also want to watch out for biased datasets that lead to biased AI outcomes.
>
> **[5:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=341)** We want to understand usage restrictions, so we want to be aware of license limits and how we can test and validate our data.
>
> **[5:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=349)** We also want to watch for pricing models that might become unsustainable as we move forward.
>
> **[5:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/identifying-data-sources?u=76281980&t=355)** And then finally, we want to consider dependencies on inconsistent data sources and make sure that we can tolerate any potential service disruptions that might occur.

#### Structured, semi-structured, and unstructured data collection
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's examine the three categories of data used in AI, structured, semi-structured, and unstructured data.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=8)** Structured data follows a fixed schema where each element has a defined format, position, and length.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=14)** This well-defined organization makes the data immediately accessible for processing.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=19)** We find structured data in relational databases where information is organized into tables and rows and columns, as well as spreadsheets and CSV files.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=28)** Some examples of structured data include customer databases that contain things like customer ID, name, and purchase history, and sales transaction records that record things like product codes, quantities, and timestamps, as well as inventory systems that track things like stock keeping units or SKUs, as well as quantities and locations.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=46)** Now, the standardized structures allow for precise queries.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=49)** For example, you can easily find all customers who purchased over $10,000 last quarter.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=55)** Semi-structured data incorporates some organizational elements, but it lacks the fixed structure of databases.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=61)** Now, this is actually a good thing because it adapts to varying information needs without requiring changes in predefined schemas.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=67)** The way it does this is because data contains tags or keys that identify what each element represents, so this makes the data interpretable without requiring external schema definitions.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=80)** Some examples of unstructured data are JSON documents, which are widely used in applications.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=85)** XML files that we often see being used for data exchange, email headers with sender recipient information, and system logs that capture event data are some other examples of semi-structured data.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=98)** Semi-structured data can maintain parent-child relationships between elements, creating nested structures that preserve logical connections.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=106)** Now, these formats combine simple values, like strings and numbers, as well as containers that hold multiple elements, and arrays of related items.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=115)** And this provides a flexibility for representing complex data structures.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=121)** Unstructured data lacks formal obvious structures and don't fit neatly into rows and columns.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=126)** Now, examples of unstructured data include things like text documents, email content, social media posts, photographs, videos, and voice recordings.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=135)** The formats can vary widely, depending on the type of data that we're using, and interpretation often requires understanding context.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=143)** So for example, there might be sarcasm in customer feedback or industry jargon in documents.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=149)** Now, to analyze unstructured data, we often find ourselves extracting specific elements, for example, sentiment scores from a customer review or facial recognition patterns from images or keyword frequencies from documents.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=163)** Now, there's a lot of business value to structured data.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=165)** Structured data powers dashboards and business intelligence tools that deliver metrics on company performance, market trends, and operational efficiency.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=175)** It also enables standardized reporting across departments, consistent measures of key performance indicators or KPIs, and comparative analysis across time periods.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=185)** Sales forecasting uses historical transaction patterns to project future revenue.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=190)** Performance analysis compares actual results against benchmarks and customer segmentation operations group clients by spending patterns, demographics, and behavior of targeted strategies.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=201)** Now, semi-structured data also has significant business value.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=205)** Semi-structured data accommodates varying attributes across product lines, regional requirements, and changing business needs without database restructuring.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=214)** It facilitates system integration across platforms, like CRM and ERP.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=219)** And organizations can use semi-structured formats to share complex information, both internally, as well as with external partners.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=228)** Now we see a lot of examples of semi-structured data.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=231)** These include things like product catalogs that use flexible schemas to handle varying attributes across different kinds of merchandise, as well as in things like IoT sensors that can transmit readings with contextual information, and web analytics, which capture both standard metrics and custom events in extensible formats.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=250)** Unstructured data is also valuable.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=252)** For example, customer reviews, support transcripts, and social media mentions contain detailed feedback that reveal not just what customers think, but why they hold these opinions.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=263)** Now, by analyzing thousands of support conversations, a company can identify recurring issues, successful strategies for resolving issues, and emerging patterns of concern before they start to adversely impact the bottom line.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=277)** Now, manufacturing lines use camera systems to detect product defects, packaging errors, and processing deviations at speeds and accuracy that are difficult for human inspectors to maintain.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=289)** Now, there are challenges with working with all of these types of data.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=293)** For example, in structured data and semi-structured data, we have issues around silos.
>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=299)** So for example, marketing, sales, and operations often maintain separate database with minimal integration, and that prevents comprehensive customer reviews and process optimization.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=310)** Older systems frequently use proprietary formats or outdated protocols that make it harder to integrate with modern analytics platforms.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=318)** Then we have data quality and consistency issues, like duplicate entries and inconsistent formatting standards across departments, as well as incomplete records.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=328)** Database structures require careful initial design, as well as ongoing updates, to accommodate new business requirements, but we have to do that in ways that don't disrupt existing operations.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=338)** Now, unstructured data has its own set of challenges.
>
> **[5:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=341)** Video, audio, and image files demand larger amounts of storage than text data.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=347)** Analyzing unstructured data requires sophisticated processing models and significant computing power.
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/structured-semi-structured-and-unstructured-data-collection?u=76281980&t=354)** Unstructured data often contains embedded sensitive information, like personal details and documents or identifiable individuals in videos, and this can create compliance challenges, especially under regulations, like GDPR in the EU or the California Consumer Privacy Act, known as CCPA.

#### Data sampling techniques and statistical considerations
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=6)** Now, the reason for this is that working with full data sets is sometimes impractical even with advanced computing resources.
>

> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=34)** It also accelerates exploration and development cycles by lowering processing requirements.

> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=39)** Sampling enables more efficient hypothesis testing across a larger data landscape, and it can be useful for identifying data quality issues before we commit to a full blown implementation.

> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=52)** Random sampling is really the gold standard for sampling.

>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=64)** We can also use systematic sampling where we select every nth item for efficiency.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=70)** Now this is, this may miss patterns, but it may be particularly useful, for example, in time series data where you don't have all of the data at one time and you have to sample over time.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=81)** Another example is stratified sampling.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=83)** And this is useful because it ensures representation across different critical business segments like different consumer segments.

>

>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=116)** We also want to take into account existing infrastructure because that can create practical boundaries on what methods we can use.

>

>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=153)** And in general, we need to balance sampling rigor, which is practical development timelines.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=160)** We also have statistical considerations.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=163)** So for example, here we wanted to consider things like what confidence level do we want to maintain?
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=169)** Oftentimes we select confidence levels based on decision criticality.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=173)** So for really critical decisions, we might want to have a 99% confidence interval, whereas if we're more tolerant, we might consider a lower confidence level such as 90 or 95%.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=188)** We want to define an acceptable margin of error to help us determine the minimum sample size.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=194)** We also want to understand that if we have a data distribution with a high data variance, we're going to require a larger sample for statistical validity.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=204)** And we also want to determine the minimum effect size needed to avoid oversampling.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=211)** Now, when it comes to testing validity, we want to use hypothesis testing that separates genuine insights from statistical noise.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=220)** So we use tools like power analysis to confirm we have sufficient sample size before proceeding.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=225)** We also want to be sure we do distribution analysis to verify that our sample is representative.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=232)** And then we also want to make sure that we define confidence intervals and use those to communicate uncertainty ranges to stakeholders.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=242)** Bias is a real problem in AI systems.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=245)** Selection bias creates unrepresented samples that can undermine the model's effectiveness.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=251)** Now there are different types of bias.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=252)** There's something called survivorship bias, which creates incomplete pictures by focusing on only the most visible cases.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=259)** We also have recency bias, which can overemphasize recent data and cause us to miss long-term patterns.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-sampling-techniques-and-statistical-considerations?u=76281980&t=266)** And then there's also availability bias, which excludes valuable but harder to collect information.

#### Workflows for automated data collection
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] We need to consider how we're going to collect data.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=3)** Enterprise data is scattered across multiple systems, making collection a fundamental challenge in these AI initiatives.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=10)** Now, manual collection processes create bottlenecks and introduce real opportunity for human error into critical data pipelines.

> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=39)** Data collection workflows provide orchestrated sequences that allow us to gather, validate, and prepare data in a systematic manner.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=48)** Collections can be triggered by multiple events, like a time interval, a specific event, or some business condition threshold.

> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=57)** Now, robust workflows include comprehensive error handling and alert notification.

> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=63)** It's important for proper implementation that we maintain detailed metadata and execution logs for both governance and for troubleshooting.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=74)** Now, workflows are made up of a few components.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=78)** Data sources, which represent the origin point where information is extracted from business systems, processing components that handle the transformation, validation, and enriching operations on collected data, and then finally, destination systems that are actually the repositories that store process data and formats appropriate for different analytical operations.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=101)** So when we're talking about data sources, we have to talk about data source connectors.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=106)** Now, database change data capture is one type of connector, and those are used when we want to identify and capture changes in operational databases.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=116)** Web scraping frameworks are used to extract structured information from websites and online platforms.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=123)** File system monitors detect new and modified files and designated directories in our file systems, while API integrations allow us to connect to SaaS applications for automated data extractions from these SaaS services.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=139)** And then if we're working in an environment with IoT devices, we can use IoT device connections to enable real-time data collection from physical sensors and equipment.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=149)** Processing components entail data validation rules that ensure data quality by enforcing business rules and technical constraints.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=158)** Processing components also entail transformation logic, which we use to convert from source formats to standardized structures that we need for analysis.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=168)** Enrichment services are used to augment the raw data with additional context from reference sources.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=174)** So for example, we might want to add names of specific cities, states, and countries in addition to a data source that might have only longitude and latitude.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=185)** Anomaly detection identifies outliers and potential data quality issues during processing.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=190)** And quality scoring can help provide additional quantitative metrics that are useful for when we're dealing with data reliability and trying to assess completeness.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=200)** Now, the destination component, or data destination, includes different types of data architectures, like data lakes, which provide low cost storage for raw unprocessed data at scale.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=213)** Data warehouses are useful for organizing structured data optimized for analytic queries, while feature stores prepare and store machine learning-ready data for model training and serving.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=225)** Across all of these different types of destination components, we have different types of catalogs and metadata repositories that maintain data lineage and discoverability data.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=237)** Now there's some design considerations we want to keep in mind.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=240)** We want to design systems with the assumptions that components will occasionally fail.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=244)** That's just the reality of the environment we operate in.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=248)** So we want to prioritize what is known as item potency so that operations can safely be repeated without duplicating data.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=256)** We also want to implement verification checks throughout the process, not just at the beginning of the process or at the end.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=263)** And we want to build comprehensive observability with metrics and logs because that'll enable us to do troubleshooting when things eventually do go wrong.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=273)** And another key thing to keep in mind is, as much as we want to automate, we also want to make sure that we maintain some level of human override capabilities for exceptional cases.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=285)** Now with regards to implementation, there's some guidance we want to keep in mind.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=288)** We want to begin by inventorying all data sources and documenting specific requirements.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=294)** And we also want to carefully select workflow technologies that match our team's skills and the needs that we actually have.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=301)** It's important to build incrementally with clearly defined success metrics for each phase.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=307)** And we want to implement robust monitoring and alerting 'cause that's going to help us catch issues before they impact downstream systems, like the completed AI model.
>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=317)** We also want to document our process and also make sure we document our learnings because that helps build organizational knowledge.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/workflows-for-automated-data-collection?u=76281980&t=324)** And then finally, we want to continuously refine based on different operational metrics that we collect.

### 2. Data Quality Frameworks

#### Data quality metrics
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-quality-metrics?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-quality-metrics?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Data quality is a significant driver to the success chances of our AI initiatives.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-quality-metrics?u=76281980&t=6)** When we're talking about data quality, we're talking about things like accuracy, which measure whether data values reflect real world values correctly.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-quality-metrics?u=76281980&t=14)** And completeness, which evaluates whether all required data elements are present.

> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-quality-metrics?u=76281980&t=30)** It's also important to validate and confirm data adheres to define business rules and format, and we want to ensure uniqueness of entities are represented without unnecessary duplication.

#### Error detection and correction methodologies
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] It's important to be able to detect data quality issues.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=3)** Now, some common data quality issues that we will likely run into are things like missing values that create gaps in analysis, and that leads to incomplete insights and potentially biased model predictions.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=16)** Outliers can distort statistical measures and trigger false anomaly alerts if they're not properly handled.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=22)** Duplication waste storage resources and creates inconsistency in aggregated metrics.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=29)** Structural errors like format inconsistencies prevent proper data integration across systems and label errors can result in misleading categorizations that compromise downstream analytics.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=42)** So how do we detect them?
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=43)** Well, there's several different ways.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=45)** One set of techniques are statistical detection methods, and these includes using statistical measures like z-scores and interquartile range, or IQR methods, to identify outliers by measuring how far those data points deviate from central tendencies.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=61)** We can also use distribution analysis to reveal unexpected patterns such as multimodal, skewed, or irregular distributions.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=69)** And then there's correlation analysis, which we can use to detect inconsistent relationships between variables that should be naturally connected.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=78)** Now, there are also rule-based detection methods.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=81)** These include using business logic validation rules to enforce domain-specific constraints according to operational requirements.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=90)** We can also use domain-specific constraint checking that apply specialized knowledge to data validation processes, and using regular expression pattern matching to ensure data adheres to predetermined formats and structures.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=105)** Machine learning also lends itself as a detection method.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=108)** We can use an algorithm known as isolation forests to efficiently identify anomalies by measuring how quickly the data points can be isolated.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=117)** We can use auto-encoders to detect unusual patterns by measuring reconstruction errors when compressing and expanding data.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=124)** And we can use clustering techniques to identify irregularities by finding data points that don't fit into expected group patterns.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=132)** Now, there's also opportunities for using manual detection methods.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=136)** For example, systematic sampling enables efficient manual inspection of representative data subsets.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=143)** Expert-led data labeling can help validate categories and classifications and ensure they meet business requirements.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=151)** Now, we can apply domain knowledge to identify contextual errors that automated systems might miss, and we can use multiple independent reviews to establish a consensus on ambiguous cases that requires some level of human judgment.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=168)** Automated correction is also an option.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=170)** Now, in that case, we can use things like imputation techniques to fill in missing values using methods ranging from simple averages to more sophisticated algorithms.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=181)** Now, normalization and standardization are transformations that correct scale issues to make features comparable for analysis and automated transformation pipelines can streamline recurring data preparation and incorporate correction into existing data workflows.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=200)** Now here's some implementation guidance with regards to detection methods.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=204)** First of all, we want to prioritize addressing errors that most significantly affect model performance and business outcomes.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=212)** We should combine both automated detection and human-in-the-loop approaches for optimal results.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=219)** We also want to maintain clear records of all detection and correction decisions for transparency and governance and for improving the process overall.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=228)** We also want to create feedback loops to systematically improve the data collection based on our different quality findings.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/error-detection-and-correction-methodologies?u=76281980&t=236)** And then we want to track business KPIs to quantify the impact of improved data quality on operational outcomes.

### 3. Data Preparation

#### Data normalization and standardization
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now let's take a look at data normalization and standardization.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=4)** Data normalization as applied to numerical values, and it reshapes numerical values so that they use a consistent scale while preserving relative relationships between numerical values.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=17)** Standardization is a complimentary technique and it typically is applied to categorical data like text data.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=23)** And it reformats data structures and representations to ensure consistency across systems.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=29)** Now these techniques improve algorithm performance by preventing features with large scales from dominating in the case of numeric values.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=37)** And standardized data formats optimize for storage efficiency and simplify the integration process.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=44)** Now, Min-Max is a type of scaling or normalization.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=48)** With Min-Max scaling, we transform values to fall within a defined range, typically zero to one.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=55)** Now this technique preserves a relationship between data points while constraining their magnitude.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=60)** So for example, transforming customer lifetime values from a range of say $10 to $50,000 to a scale of zero to one enables fair segmentation.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=71)** Now, Min-Max works best when the actual minimum and maximum bounds are known and are actually meaningful.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=78)** Z-score standardization rescales data to have a mean of zero and a standard deviation of one.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=86)** Now this approach highlights how far each value deviates from the population average.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=92)** This is particularly valuable for comparing things like store performance across a location with vastly different sales volumes.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=100)** Now, Z-scores maintain the statistical relationship between variables while eliminating the effects of different measurement scales.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=108)** Now let's take a look at data standardization.
>

>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=198)** So that distorts absolute metrics.
>

>

>

>

>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=237)** We can also standardize format classifications to ensure that we're making like-for-like comparisons.
>

>

>

>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=284)** Now another important factor is, like so much in planning for AI, this is not a one-time operation.
>

>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=302)** Also, we may need to update normalization methods based on how the business is evolving and business rules are changing.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=310)** So that leads to the final implementation guidance, which is one of the most important, which is again, we want to document all of our approaches.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-normalization-and-standardization?u=76281980&t=318)** So all of our normalization and standardization approaches should be documented to ensure that we have consistent application and that people who are interpreting the data actually understand what standardizations and normalizations were applied.

#### Handling missing data and outliers
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Missing data and outliers are two challenges that we have to address early in our planning stages.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=7)** Let's start with missing data.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=9)** Now, missing data is simply values that should be in your dataset but aren't.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=13)** Now, there are a variety of reasons for this.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=16)** There could be collection errors that happen when system fails or processes break.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=21)** There are also times, say for example, when customers or users opt out of sharing information.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=28)** There can also be issues when you're actually working with multiple datasets and you're trying to merge or join them and they have different structures.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=35)** That can lead to incomplete records.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=39)** Also, there's problems with older systems that weren't really built to capture the data that we need now, so it may just not exist within these systems that we're using as our data sources.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=50)** Now, in addition to missing data, we also need to deal with outliers.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=54)** Now, outliers are data points that essentially stick out from the crowd.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=58)** Now, these are important to identify because they can significantly impact your analysis and sometimes mislead decisions.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=66)** Now, there are different types of outliers.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=68)** We can basically categorize them as valid outliers, which are rare but genuine real events that have potential insights in them, so we want to make sure we keep those.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=78)** And then we could also have error outliers.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=81)** These come from mistakes, and those are the ones that need to be fixed.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=85)** What we don't want to do, though, is remove legitimate outliers because then we risk removing some important edge cases that might provide insight.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=95)** Now, there's different ways of detecting missing data.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=98)** We can use data profiling to help spot patterns of missing data.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=103)** Visualization techniques can help show gaps and help us understand are those random gaps or is there some kind of pattern that might be occurring in the dataset?
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=113)** Now, we can also use statistical techniques like correlation analysis to find related factors that correlate or correspond to missing data.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=124)** Now, when we do have missing data, there's different ways we can handle those records.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=129)** Now, the simplest fix is to simply remove records that do have missing values.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=134)** Now, that works when the data's randomly missing and you have a lot of records to work with.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=139)** Now, this has certain advantages.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=141)** First of all, it's simple, but there are some drawbacks.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=144)** I mean, we could lose critical information, so we need to be careful about losing information because that could potentially introduce bias into our AI models.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=154)** Now, imputation is an alternative technique to deleting data.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=159)** So rather than delete a record because some of the columns or some of the attributes are missing is we can fill in the missing value.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=165)** We can make educated guesses as to what the value should be.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=169)** Now, there are different ways to do that.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=170)** We could use the mean, median, or mode to replace the missing value, and we calculate mean, median, and mode based on other values in that, for example, in that column, and we use these statistical techniques to impute a value.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=185)** We can also use machine learning to predict missing values.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=190)** Now, these advanced techniques may possibly create multiple values or multiple possible values, and that's actually useful because we could, for example, assign certainty factors to each of the possible values, and then we could choose among those.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=204)** Now, with regards to outliers, there are different ways of handling outliers.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=210)** First of all, we can detect using different types of methods.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=213)** We can use statistical approaches like z-scores and IQRs, or interquartile ranges.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=219)** We can use visualizations like box plots and scatter plots to help us see visually what data points are really falling outside of, say, the main clusters or the main groups of data.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=231)** We can also use machine learning techniques like Isolation Forest that work well for complex datasets.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=237)** But one thing we want to do when we're working with outliers, we always want to pair automated detection with human review.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=244)** Now, how we go about handling outliers again varies.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=248)** We can keep the outliers in the dataset.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=251)** That's really important if those outliers represent some real business situation.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=257)** Those outliers are actually quite helpful.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=259)** They're really valuable in terms of training a model to understand how to handle unusual but genuine business scenarios.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=267)** Now, we could eliminate or remove the outlier value, and that's clearly the appropriate thing to do when that outlier is a result of an error or it really skews the analysis for some reason.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=281)** Now, there is a third method for handling outliers, which is to apply mathematical functions to reduce the outlier influence.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=289)** But we have to be careful with that, and it has to be done guided by an understanding of the business context.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=297)** So, some guidance for implementation when it comes to dealing with missing data and outliers is, first of all, we want to measure how much missing or outlier data we have.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=308)** And we want to look for patterns because that can help us identify root causes for this and help us address the problem going forward.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=315)** We also want to estimate the business impact of missing data and outliers and make sure we address the most important or the most impactful missing data or outliers.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=326)** And then, of course, it's always important to document what you're doing and why.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/handling-missing-data-and-outliers?u=76281980&t=331)** And then finally, we want to make sure we keep monitoring because as new data issues emerge, we might have new types of outliers or other kinds of missing data that we need to address.
