#### Data augmentation techniques
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] We use data augmentation to help us create additional data.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=5)** So data augmentation is a process of artificially expanding a data set by creating modified versions of the existing data.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=13)** This helps us expand our training data without collecting new raw data.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=17)** And that's important because that allows the model to handle more scenarios and more variation.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=23)** So there are multiple business value benefits to this.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=27)** It improves how well the model generalizes to new situations.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=31)** It helps reduce overfitting, where we're getting too close to the data and not generalizing enough.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=37)** And that's especially problematic when your data set is small, and it's also more cost effective than collecting additional data sets from scratch.
>

>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=67)** That is, SMOTE allows us to create synthetic examples of the minority class or the class that doesn't show up as much.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=74)** Think of fraudulent transactions in a data set of all credit card transactions.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=80)** We can also use just random value perturbation, so basically tweaking numbers within some realistic bounds.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=86)** And we can even apply statistical modeling to generate completely new but plausible records.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=93)** Text augmentation comes in different forms.

> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=95)** We can start with lexical text augmentation.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=98)** Here, we can do things like swap words with synonyms using a thesauri or word embeddings.
>

>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=116)** Now we can also augment data by applying syntactic transformations.
>

>

>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=159)** And that helps to increase diversity in the dataset.

>

>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-augmentation-techniques?u=76281980&t=177)** So these techniques can help generate high quality variations fairly quickly.

>

>

#### Feature engineering and selection
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Feature engineering and feature selection is another aspect of working with data for AI initiatives.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=8)** Now, feature engineering is the process of creating new variables from existing data to boost model performance.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=15)** Feature selection is a process of identifying and using only the most relevant variables.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=21)** Now these processes transform raw data into more predictive signals, and good features with strong signals can often make a significant difference in the quality of the models that we're able to build.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=36)** So let's look at just some examples of features in say the retail context.

>

>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=81)** Now there are different types of features.

>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=93)** And these can include features like days since last purchase that can help predict churn and engagement.
>

>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=108)** There are also temporal features we can derive around seasonal buying cycles, and that can help predict future demands.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=117)** Another temporal feature that's important in inventory management is days to reorder.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=121)** That helps optimize inventory and also market timing.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=126)** Now there are also features that we can derive by aggregating values.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=131)** So for example, we can aggregate or find the aggregate function of the average basket size, and maybe we find average basket size by different customer segment type, because that can help reveal different spending patterns across different customer groups.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=146)** We can also look at product category affinities, which show which departments tend to be shopped for together.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=153)** And we can also work with the percentage of spending by department because that helps identify customer preferences and interests.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=162)** So in general, aggregations transform individual transactions into more meaningful kind of profiles at a higher level of aggregation, say customer segment as opposed to an individual customer.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=174)** Now there's also interaction features we might want to engineer.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=179)** Now these include things like product co-purchase frequencies which reveal which products drive sales of other products.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=186)** We also want to look at promotion responses by segment 'cause that can show us which offers work for which specific type of customer.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=195)** There's also ways of identifying price sensitivity and promotion type to capture complex purchasing behaviors.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=202)** Now, in addition to engineering features, when we want to add additional features to help our model, we also want to think about eliminating features that aren't adding value.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=213)** And we use feature selection methods for that.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=217)** Now, one method is called correlation analysis and that helps eliminate redundant variables that don't really add new information.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=224)** Now we can use statistical tests to identify which features have significant relationships with a target variable we're interrogating.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=232)** And we can also do incremental testing to add or remove features one at a time and measure their impact.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=240)** There are also statistical techniques known as regularization techniques such as lasso and ridge that automatically shrink or eliminate weaker features.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=251)** And then finally, we can also use expert opinion to ensure that business-relevant features are included and not inappropriately disregarded in feature selection operations.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=264)** So when you're implementing feature engineering and feature selection, here are some things to keep in mind.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=271)** First of all, you want to prioritize features with clear business meaning, over kind of black box variables that aren't really well understood.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=279)** You'll also want to document all transformations so that end users and anyone interpreting the data and the models can understand and possibly reproduce your work if needed.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=290)** You also want to build automated pipelines.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=293)** And again, we want to consistently apply what we're focused on.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=296)** In this case, feature engineering and feature selection.
>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=299)** We want to be able to consistently apply those operations in production.
>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=303)** We also want to test on historical data to validate the usefulness before fully implementing some of our ideas around feature engineering and feature selection.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=314)** Now we also want to use cross validation to prevent overfitting.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=318)** So we don't want to so engineer the selection of features and our engineered or new features that we're adding, so that we are essentially memorizing the training set.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=328)** Because that's what we can do if we overfit.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=333)** And then finally, we want to monitor for feature drift over time, because customer's behaviors will change, the market will change, business conditions will change.
>
> **[5:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-engineering-and-selection?u=76281980&t=343)** So we want to make sure we are detecting those changes and capturing the relevance of new information in our selected features and our engineered features.

### 4. AI Storage Systems

#### Types of storage systems: Object storage
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] We use a variety of types of storage in AI applications.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=4)** One of the most important is object storage.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=7)** Now, with object storage, we treat data as self-contained units rather than files in a hierarchical system.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=14)** Each object bundles the data itself, as well as metadata about it and a unique identifier.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=21)** Object storage uses a flat address space instead of folders and directories, so there's no hierarchical structure.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=29)** And typically, we access object storage using APIs, like standard HTTP protocols.

>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=47)** Now, there are several key features of object storage.
>

>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=57)** Also, there's essentially no practical capacity limits.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=61)** We don't need to add storage or nodes as our need increases.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=66)** And another feature of object storage is that it is able to maintain consistent performance regardless of how much data we're storing.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=75)** And object storage provides built-in redundancy and automatically replicates data across regions if we choose multi-region support.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=85)** And the best solutions have very high durability, what are considered 11 nines durability in the top solution.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=93)** So, it's highly unlikely that we would be unable to read data.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=99)** Now, object storage is also highly cost-effective because it's uses a pay-as-you-go model, which means you only pay for the actual storage you use.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=107)** And it often comes structured with storage tiers that lets you balance access speed versus cost.

>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=128)** That's not the case when we're working with object storage in a cloud provider.
>

>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-object-storage?u=76281980&t=143)** And this data actually enables us to build sophisticated lifecycle data management and government policies within the object storage system.

>

#### Types of storage systems: Block and file storage
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] File storage and block storage are two additional types of storage system that are crucial in AI systems.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=7)** Let's take a look at file storage first.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=10)** File stores use folders and directories in a hierarchical structure, and files are accessed through familiar paths.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=17)** So for example, we might have a directory name with sub directories followed by a slash and another subdirectory name.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=24)** Now, we also have a number of different protocols like NFS and SMB that are widely used as well as some more specialized protocols like Google File Store.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=36)** Now, file storage is most intuitive for users who are accustomed to working with traditional computing environments, desktop devices, and so on.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=45)** Now, block storage is a different type of storage.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=48)** Block storage splits data into fixed size blocks, each with a unique address.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=54)** And now operating systems access this raw storage directly.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=58)** And this is ideal when you want to deliver high performance with minimal latency.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=62)** Now, there are different examples of block storage protocols like SAN or AWS, EBS, or Azure Disk Storage, as well as Google Persistent Disk.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=72)** And these are ideal for applications that require consistent IO performance.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=79)** Now, file storage is crucial in AI workflows for a number of reasons.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=83)** It provides for interactive access for data scientists during development.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=89)** It's also used for code repositories in Jupyter Notebooks, commonly used by data scientists, and it integrates directly with popular machine learning frameworks, and it offers simple data management through familiar directory structures.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=104)** So file storage is important in AI workflows because they deliver fast, consistent access that's needed for real time applications.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=113)** Now, block storage is also important in AI workflows.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=117)** Block storage is ideal for structured AI metadata that requires transactional integrity.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=124)** Now we can use block storage with feature stores that need reliable transaction processing.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=130)** It also provides fast consistent IO for relational databases supporting AI systems.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=136)** In addition, block storage enables high speed local caching for models for quick access, and it's critical for low latency access in time sensitive inference scenarios.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=148)** Now, when we're comparing storage systems, it can help to think of all three types that we've discussed.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=155)** Object storage, file storage, and block storage.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=158)** So file storage excels with regards to development and working with medium sized datasets.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=163)** Block storage is ideal for high performance computing and database workloads.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=169)** Object storage is really well-suited for large data sets and distributed training.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=175)** When it comes to performance, expect the best performance by block storage, followed by file storage, and then object storage.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=182)** With regards to scalability, object storage really stands out among all three as by far the best.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=189)** In terms of shared access, object storage is really easy because it's universally accessible, but file storage is relatively easily shared as well.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=197)** Block storage is definitely not easily shared.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=201)** So when you're choosing a particular storage system that you want to use for a particular component in your AI system, you want to think about these different kinds of workload requirements and characteristics or features of each of the types of data storage.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=216)** Now, some things to keep in mind, each storage type really serves a distinct role within the overall AI workflow and support environment.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=226)** File storage handles development environments and active workloads.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=230)** Block storage is really the foundation for performance critical computing and databases, while object storage manages massive data lakes and model registries.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-block-and-file-storage?u=76281980&t=242)** Now, modern AI pipelines typically benefit from a hybrid mixed approach that combines all three data types.

>

>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=98)** Now, ACID itself stands for animosity, consistency, isolation, and durability.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=104)** Now, atomicity ensures operations are all or nothing.

>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=110)** Consistency is about maintaining data validity according to some predefined set of rules.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=116)** Isolation is important because it keeps concurrent operations separate, so we don't have two operations that are running at the same time interfering with each other.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=127)** Durability is an important characteristic because that's what guarantees that committed data persist even during system failures.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=135)** And all of these together are critical for transaction applications.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=141)** Now, another set of key features are oriented around query optimization, which represents a significant advantage for database systems over other storage systems like raw file storage.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=152)** These query systems include built-in query planners that automatically determine the most efficient execution path for retrieving data, as well as caching mechanisms that can store frequently accessed data 'cause that can help with faster retrieval.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=166)** They also maintain statistics because that helps inform execution plan development so we can make more intelligent processing decisions.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=176)** There's also support for programming interfaces, which allow for integration with application code.
>

>

>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=200)** They use SQL as a standardized query language even across different implementations.

>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=214)** And also, relational databases have been around for a long time.
>

>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=223)** Now, another type of database are NoSQL databases, and NoSQL databases emerge to address some of the limitations of relational databases, at least with regards to certain workloads.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=234)** Now, there are different types of NoSQL databases, document databases like MongoDB and Couchbase store semi-structured data in flexible formats.
>

>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=252)** While column-family databases like Cassandra excel at handling really massive distributed data sets.
>

>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=267)** Now, we can use relational databases and no SQL databases for different use cases.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=273)** Now, in AI and machine learning, one popular use case is something known as a feature store.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=280)** Feature stores represent specialized database systems designed specifically for machine learning workflows.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=286)** They provide version control for tracking changes to feature definitions over time.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=292)** Feature stores enable consistent transformation pipelines, and that ensures that features are processed identically, whether it's in training or in production.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=302)** They're also efficient at serving and optimizing both batch training and real-time inference scenarios.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=310)** Some examples of feature store our Feast, Tecton, and Amazon SageMaker's feature store.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=316)** Now, another use case for databases is model metadata management.
>
> **[5:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=320)** When we talk about models here, we're talking about machine learning models or AI models.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=325)** Now, model metadata management tracks the entire lifecycle of AI models.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=331)** They store model version, parameters, and other artifacts that are important for being able to reproduce that model.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=339)** And so, it includes things like training run history, which captures the progression of the model over time, experiment tracking facilities, which are useful for comparing between different modeling approaches, lineage tracking for deployed models, and that's useful for creating audit trails, especially for regulatory compliance.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=358)** Now, popular tools around model metadata management include platforms like MLFlow, and Weights & Biases, which integrate with most ML frameworks.
>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=369)** Now, vector databases is another use case for databases in AI.
>
> **[6:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=374)** Vector databases represent a specialized category of database optimized for similarity-based searches over unstructured data.
>
> **[6:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=383)** They efficiently support operations on high-dimensional vectors, which are fundamental to modern AI, especially when working with unstructured data like text, video, and audio.
>
> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=393)** These systems are essential for application embeddings, which is how we represent those unstructured data types for machine learning applications, and they form the core infrastructure for semantic search systems.
>
> **[6:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=408)** Now, some examples include Pinecone, Milvus, and the pgvector extension in PostgreSQL.
>
> **[6:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=417)** So, when do we use databases in AI?
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=419)** Well, first of all, we choose database storage when we have applications within our AI workflow that require complex query requirements.
>
> **[7:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=429)** We also use it when transaction support is essential, for example, when we're dealing with multiple operations that have to succeed or fail together.
>
> **[7:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=436)** We also use databases when data relationships need to be maintained and enforced.
>
> **[7:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=442)** We also use databases when robust data integrity requirements are important.
>
> **[7:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=448)** Now, advanced indexing is important as well when we are looking for performance optimization.
>
> **[7:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=455)** Also, high-concurrency workloads where there may be many users or processes trying to access data simultaneously is a leading indicator or a good indicator that we probably want to be using a database for that use case.
>
> **[7:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=469)** So, some things to keep in mind when you're working with databases is you want to match your type of database to your specific workload characteristics.
>
> **[7:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=476)** We also want to consider current and future scaling requirements when you're designing your database architecture.
>
> **[8:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=482)** Evaluate managed database services versus self-hosted options based on your team's experience and your tolerance for having to perform database management operations yourself.
>
> **[8:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=494)** Plan comprehensive backup and recovery strategies, and implement appropriate security controls.
>
> **[8:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=500)** Now, this should include authentication, authorization, and encryption.
>
> **[8:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/types-of-storage-systems-databases?u=76281980&t=504)** And then, finally, be sure you establish monitoring for key performance metrics to identify any issues before they start to impact users.

### 5. AI Processing Infrastructure

#### Batch processing systems
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] We process data in AI using different processing patterns, one of which is called batch processing.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=6)** This is where we process large volumes of data in predefined groups rather than continuously.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=12)** Batch processing is optimized for throughput over immediate response, so we often schedule executions using pre allocated resources.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=23)** And really batch processing is the foundation for training large AI models and processing massive data sets.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=29)** Now, batch processing has been around for a long time, so it's a fairly mature paradigm and it has some well established tools and frameworks.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=38)** Some key characteristics of batch processing include the ways that data is collected, stored, and processed, which is in discrete batches.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=47)** Now, the processing occurs at scheduled intervals or based on certain events or triggered by certain conditions.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=55)** The nice thing about batch processing and the way it's triggered is that we have some predictability, so we have predictable resource allocation based on batch size, and we know when batches will be run.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=67)** Now we need to keep in mind that the results of a batch processing are typically only available when the entire batch process completes.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=75)** This makes batch processing well suited for non-time sensitive AI workloads.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=81)** Now, AI training is a prime example.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=83)** We may, for example, have large neural network training on fairly large historical data sets, or we might have periodic model retraining as we accumulate new data.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=93)** We also use batch processing for hyper parameter optimization, and we do this typically through sequential runs.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=101)** We also use batch processing when we do cross validation for comprehensive model evaluation.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=108)** Data preparation is another workload or pattern where batch processing makes sense.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=113)** We use ETL or extraction transformation and load processes for creating training sets.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=119)** And we also use batch processing for feature engineering at scale when we're working with say, millions of records.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=126)** Also, if we have a comprehensive data cleansing and normalization operation, or if we're running training validation and test generation, we would want to use batch processing.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=137)** We can also use batch processing when we're working with complex engineered feature calculations.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=144)** Now, when we're talking about the architecture or the technical architecture of batch processing, we may want to use a distributed computing platform like Spark or Hadoop.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=154)** We also want to take advantage of accelerators like GPUs and TPUs and use those with clusters, especially when we're working with neural network training.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=163)** Batch processing involves jobs, and so job scheduling system for research management is an important tool that we want to have in our technical architecture.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=173)** We also want to make sure we're working with storage systems that are optimized for large sequential reads.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=179)** There are several benefits that come with batch processing, the first of which is cost efficiency, and we get that through optimized resource utilization.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=189)** We can also take advantage of off peak processing, which sometimes have lower cost and more availability with regards to our computing resources.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=198)** Batch processing allows us to do fairly predictable budgeting and resource allocation, and there's also some more operational stability because with batch processing, we can have clearly defined maintenance windows.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=212)** And also batch processing allows for more simplified monitoring and troubleshooting than we might have if we're working with, say, a stream processing model, which we'll talk about shortly.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=222)** Now, when it comes to implementing batch processing, you want to start with well-defined smaller workloads before scaling them up.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=229)** You want to be sure as you're defining your workloads that you design for failure recovery, and one of the ways to do this is to use what we call checkpointing or saving results intermittently, so you can roll back or start with one of those checkpoints rather than going all the way back to the beginning of the workload.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=247)** We also want to implement comprehensive logging and monitoring and be sure that we establish automated quality checks on both the original data and intermittent steps in the process.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/batch-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=258)** And then finally, we want to balance batch size against processing time and resources.

#### Stream processing systems
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Stream processing is an alternative to batch processing.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=4)** Now, stream processing analyzes data in real time as it arrives rather than waiting to process it in batches.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=10)** So it's really designed specifically to minimize latency.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=15)** So then unlike batch processing, it handles each data point or maybe small micro batches individually as those data points or micro batches flow through the system.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=25)** Now this allows AI systems to react to events instantly rather than waiting for, like, a scheduled processing time to arrive.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=34)** Stream processing has really become essential for applications where small delays could really adversely impact business outcomes or our user experience.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=44)** Stream processing works with continuous data flows, which don't have really well-defined start or endpoints.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=50)** Now, the technology that deliver these really extremely fast response time are often measured in milliseconds rather than seconds, minutes, or hours.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=61)** Now, modern stream processing platforms help maintain context and state across multiple data points, so that allows us to do more sophisticated analysis than we might otherwise be able to do.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=75)** The architectures of stream processing systems are fundamentally event-driven, which means the processing is triggered by when data arrives rather than, you know, when the clock hits a certain time or when it's time to schedule a particular job.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=89)** Now these systems are built for continuous operation, so they're really designed for application use cases that have high availability requirements.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=99)** We see stream processing in a number of different kinds of AI applications.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=103)** For example, recommendation engines use stream processing for instantly updating suggestions based on, say, your most recent clicks or your most recent views.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=114)** We also need low latency for fraud detection, so we can, for example, flag suspicious transactions immediately before the transaction is actually processed.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=125)** Now, streaming is also useful, say, in manufacturing operations, where you can use stream processing with equipment sensors to help predict maintenance needs before a failure actually occurs.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=138)** Now, self-driving cars and autonomous vehicles are systems that depend on stream processing because they really have very short periods of time to make decisions.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=147)** And then maybe for slightly longer timeframes, we have things like conversational AI applications.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=153)** You know, it's not as time sensitive as, say, an autonomous vehicle, but we still want to use stream processing to analyze and respond to natural language inputs without long delays.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=163)** Now, when we think about the technical components that go into making up a stream processing system, we want to have an event streaming platform.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=171)** And some of the most popular are known as Kafka, Kinesis, and Pulsar.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=176)** Processing frameworks such as Spark Streaming, Flink, and Samza are sort of the computational engines that transform raw data into transform data.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=187)** We'll also want to make use of in-memory computing techniques for maintaining state information.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=191)** And this is important because we don't want to slow down operations by accessing data on a disc.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=196)** We need to have it available in very fast access formats.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=202)** Now sometimes we have to send messages between components.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=205)** In that case, we want to use low-latency messaging systems.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=208)** Those can ensure minimal delays between the times we are able to do processing in the different components.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=214)** And then we also want distributed fault-tolerant processing clusters that can provide all of the necessary basically computational power that we're going to need for the amount of data that's actually streaming in.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=228)** Now we also want to think about how data flows through these systems, and so we want to think about functionally, what are the components that we need from a data flow perspective?
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=238)** Well, we need things that are essentially operated as source connectors that capture events from various source systems like APIs or IoT devices, and then transform those data into standardized streams.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=252)** We also want to have stream processors that handle the core work.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=256)** So these are the computational platforms.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=258)** And they do things like executing AI inference and applying business logic to incoming data in real time.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=265)** We also may want to access online feature stores to provide fast access to pre-computed features that we need for model inference.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=272)** Sometimes we need state back ends, and this is used for maintaining contextual information between events.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=278)** And this is really important when we have more sophisticated processing logic that we need to implement.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=284)** And then finally, we need something known as sink connectors.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=287)** These are the components that will basically deliver the process results and predictions to whatever downstream applications are consuming the output of our stream.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=297)** Now, the benefits of stream processing include the ability to deliver immediate response to changing conditions, and this rapid insight generation can create competitive advantages when we're dealing with time-sensitive operations or applications.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=312)** It's also useful because models can continuously learn and adapt from streaming data, and this can help with improving accuracy without long drawn out retraining cycles.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=323)** Also, we can improve customer experience by improving real-time personalization that responds to the current context rather than just historical patterns we might have analyzed in a batch mode.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=335)** Also, we can detect problems and address them more efficiently, oftentimes before they significantly adversely impact, say, an operation or a customer experience.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=347)** When you're implementing stream processing, you want to start by identifying specific use cases where real-time processing can deliver, like, clear business value.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=358)** We also want to implement comprehensive monitoring here.
>
> **[6:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=361)** I know I keep mentioning monitoring, but that is just so fundamentally important.
>
> **[6:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=365)** If we're not able to track the health of our system, especially with stream processing, we're not going to be able to deliver the benefits of stream processing.
>
> **[6:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=374)** We also want to make sure that we design for failure.
>
> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=377)** Our architecture should be designed to degrade gracefully under heavy loads rather than completely falling over because we have, like, an unusually or unexpected spike in traffic.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=387)** We also want to make sure we have robust error handling using things like dead-letter queues to catch and manage problematic data without clogging up the entire pipeline.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=397)** And then finally, we want to make sure that we're balancing processing complexity and latency requirements.
>
> **[6:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=404)** The more complex our processing, the longer we'll have to take to actually perform that computation, and that can drive up the latency.
>
> **[6:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/stream-processing-systems?u=76281980&t=411)** So, again, we're dealing with a balancing act here of how much complexity we want to implement versus what's the latency that we can tolerate before we have to have an answer and deliver some data to the downstream systems.
