#### Scaling AI processing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Whether we're using batch processing or stream processing, we want to think about how we're going to scale our AI systems.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=8)** Now successfully transitioning AI's application, say from a prototype or proof of concept to a production system, often requires comprehensive scaling strategies that go beyond simply throwing more hardware at the problem.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=21)** As models grow in complexity and the data volumes expand, the processing demands just don't increase linearly, they could grow much more rapidly than that.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=31)** So effective scaling requires us to think about both the computational aspects and the architectural design of our systems 'cause our goal here, we need to find the right balance between performance capabilities, the cost of the infrastructure that we're running and the operational complexity of that infrastructure.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=49)** Now this balance becomes increasingly critical as the usage grows since maintaining acceptable response times and throughput directly impacts user experience.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=61)** Now it's important to think about scaling dimensions or how do we go about scaling?
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=65)** One way of scaling is called vertical scaling, and that involves essentially increasing the compute power of individual nodes.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=72)** For example, adding more virtual CPUs or adding more memory.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=76)** So basically we're betting on bigger, more powerful machines.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=81)** Horizontal scaling takes a different tact by adding more processing nodes to distribute the workload across multiple machines, rather than increasing the resources on a single machine.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=93)** We also want to think about being able to operate on data in parallel.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=97)** So data parallelism divides our dataset across multiple processors, each of which can handle a portion of the data.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=105)** Similarly, we can think about model parallelism, which distributes different parts of the model across different computing resources.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=113)** And that's particularly useful when the model's too large to fit on a single device.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=118)** And then we also want to think about pipeline parallelism.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=121)** This is where we execute different processing stages simultaneously.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=126)** Now we have different infrastructure options when we're thinking about scaling.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=130)** We can have on-premise infrastructure.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=132)** For example, we could have high performance computing clusters in our on-premise data center.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=136)** And that has the advantage of giving us complete control.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=140)** However, that does require significant capital investment and also expertise in operating the clusters.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=146)** We can avoid some of the capital costs and some of the expertise requirements by moving to cloud-based AI infrastructure.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=153)** And another advantage of going to the cloud is that with the cloud we have more flexibility with regards to scaling up or scaling down according to our needs.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=164)** Also in the cloud, we have access to specialized hardware accelerators that we may not have on-prem, like large arrays of GPUs, TPUs, floating point gate arrays, or other accelerators.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=176)** We also may want to take advantage of edge computing.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=180)** Edge computing is where we move AI processing closer to where the debt is generated, and that can help reduce latency for time sensitive applications.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=188)** Oftentimes we benefit from using hybrid architecture where we combine multiple types of these infrastructures to balance performance and cost requirements.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=198)** Now, when it comes to scaling up AI training, we often want to think in terms of distributed training and spreading workloads across multiple nodes using data parallelism.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=210)** We can also use some AI specific techniques like mixed precision training, which uses lower precision formats like say 16 bit floating point rather than like 32 or 64 bit floating point.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=222)** Now that can increase computational throughput without really significantly adversely impacting the accuracy of the model.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=229)** We also want to make sure we're using checkpointing.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=232)** And we mentioned this with like with batch processing.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=234)** Checkpointing allows us to save the model state here at regular intervals, and this gives us a little bit more resilience in case there's a failure at some point in the pipeline.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=244)** We also want to think about running multiple hyper parameter optimization experiments in parallel so that we can find our optimal model configuration faster than if we were to run say each of those hyper parameter optimization experiments, one after the other.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=260)** Now we also want to think about scaling inferencing In addition to scaling training.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=265)** When we're talking about scaling inferencing, we might want to use what's known as quantization.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=271)** Now, model quantization reduces the computational requirements of a particular model by converting some of those floating point weights that we learned during the training session to lower precision formats.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=283)** And again, this we do it in ways that has minimal impact on accuracy.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=289)** We can also use a process called distillation.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=291)** Now, model distillation creates smaller, faster, which you can think of as like student models that learned from the larger teacher model while still maintaining reasonable performance of the student model.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=304)** We can also use batching of multiple prediction requests together, and that can maximize the throughput by better utilizing the hardware's parallel processing capabilities.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=316)** Dynamic serving allocation adjust resources based on traffic patterns.
>
> **[5:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=320)** So for example, we can auto scale up during peak times and then scale down when there's less demand.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=326)** And we may also want to employ prediction caching stores.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=329)** Now this is useful when we have common inputs and we need to generate the same type of output over and over again 'cause that can eliminate unnecessary computation for frequently requested predictions.
>
> **[5:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=341)** Of course, we want to think about performance monitoring.
>
> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=344)** So we want to be sure we're tracking end-to-end latency.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=347)** So we want to be sure to measure, for example, how long it takes a request from the time we get the input to the time we actually produce useful output.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=356)** And we also want to measure latency at different components because that can help identify bottlenecks across the pipeline.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=363)** We also want to make sure we are capturing throughput measurements that tell us like how many requests our system is able to handle, say per minute or per second.
>
> **[6:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=373)** We also want to think in terms of resource utilization.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=376)** So we want to track things like CPU, memory. I/O or IOPS, as well as network usage.
>
> **[6:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=383)** And when it comes to production models, we want to make sure we have performance metrics that help us detect things like concept drift or data quality issues that might slowly degrade the model's performance.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=397)** When you're implementing your scaling strategy, you want to begin with thorough benchmarking.
>
> **[6:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=402)** It's important that we understand the specific scaling requirements of our particular applications.
>
> **[6:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=407)** Just because one application has a certain set of scaling requirements, another application might not have similar requirements.
>
> **[6:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=415)** Also designed for horizontal scaling from the beginning, even if you don't need it right away.
>
> **[7:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=420)** Be sure to implement comprehensive monitoring and alerting systems.
>
> **[7:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=425)** And make sure you adopt infrastructure as code practices.
>
> **[7:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=428)** Those are really important to help ensuring that our deployments are consistent and reproducible.
>
> **[7:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=433)** And then finally, we want to design fallback mechanisms for graceful degradation.
>
> **[7:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/scaling-ai-processing?u=76281980&t=438)** We want to be able to essentially maintain as much core functionality as we can, even when our resources are constrained.

### 6. Optimizing AI Process Workflows

#### Metadata management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Metadata is structured information that describes, explains, and help us locate our AI assets.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=7)** Now with metadata, we are able to effectively discover, organize, and understand these different assets that we have.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=15)** Now, proper metadata management is also critical for governance compliance and basically ensuring that our AI processes are reproducible.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=23)** Now, when we implement metadata management correctly, we can use that metadata to basically help us implement efficient data access patterns and do things like discover intelligent caching mechanisms that might be most effective.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=39)** We can think of metadata as the foundation that makes automated AI workflow orchestration even possible at the scales we need to operate at.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=48)** There are different types of metadata associated with AI.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=52)** There's technical metadata that describes sort of the basics of our implementation.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=57)** Things like file formats, schemas, and where the data is physically stored.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=62)** There's also operational metadata that captures information about the steps in our data processing pipelines, and these include things like the processing history, our lineage, and version information.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=74)** When it comes to business metadata, we're talking about data in an organizational context, like the ownership or the purpose or the sensitivity of particular data that we might be working with.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=88)** Quality metadata is useful when we want to quantify how reliable our data is or capture metrics about accuracy and completeness of our data.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=99)** There's also usage metadata that reveals information about how people interact with the data and shows us things like access patterns and popularity of different subsets of data, as well as things like performance statistics.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=113)** Now there are architecture considerations when we're working with metadata.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=117)** Metadata repositories, we need to remember, provide a centralized storage system and management capabilities, and these become essentially our centralized single source of truth for metadata.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=129)** We often want to have automated ingestion pipelines that are continuously capturing metadata throughout the AI workflows.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=138)** We also want to be sure that our classification and tagging engines are consistent in how they tag and categorize assets.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=147)** We also want to be sure that we have capabilities around search and discovery so that we can make the metadata that we capture actually accessible and useful for both technical and business users.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=160)** And we want to think about integration points within the workflow and orchestration flows so that we allow metadata to actually inform and guide our AI processes.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=173)** So one way to do this is making sure that we have a data catalog for AI.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=178)** Now, what we want to do is automatically discover and continuously scan for and classify AI-related datasets across our organization.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=188)** Once we've identified those, we want to apply semantic tags.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=192)** Now, these go beyond basic labels because semantic tags can help enhance searchability and help us understand complex datasets and the relationships between those datasets.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=203)** We want to make sure we have a business glossary that we can integrate into our platform so that we improve the consistency with which we use different terminology.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=214)** Now, data profiling tools are also important for capturing statistical properties about our datasets.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=221)** And collaborative annotation tools allow domain experts to contribute really important business context to technical datasets, and we want to make sure we capture those in our data catalog as well.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=234)** Lineage tracking is a type of metadata that allows us to capture traceability from the raw data that we use to the model deployment.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=245)** And this is important 'cause it helps us provide robust audit capabilities to support compliance and government requirements.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=253)** Lineage tracking also helps us with an impact analysis and it allows us to understand complex dependency chains and helps us understand how a change might affect downstream systems.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=265)** Now, in a production system, problems are going to arise.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=269)** And then when that happens, comprehensive lineage tracking can help us troubleshoot and help us identify quickly where problems originated.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=278)** Now, model metadata is another type of metadata that we want to capture.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=283)** Now, with regards to models, we'll want to capture version control information and parameters that help us ensure we can recreate a version of the model at any time.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=293)** We also want to track performance metrics across different iterations or different versions so that helps the development teams understand how different changes to the models are affecting outcomes.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=305)** We also want training dataset metadata 'cause that can provide critical provenance information and linking information as well.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=315)** And it's also important that we have detailed hyperparameter metadata and hyperparameter documentation to ensure that we can reproduce training runs.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=325)** Now, as you're thinking about implementing metadata, you want to start with clear metadata standards and governance policies.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=332)** And we want to work toward implementing automated capture mechanisms at each stage of the workflow.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=338)** We also want to strike the right balance between metadata detail and management overhead.
>
> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=344)** We don't want to become so focused on capturing every bit of metadata that we can possibly capture that our metadata management processes become unwieldy.
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=354)** And we also want to integrate as much as possible our metadata collection with our existing data governance practices 'cause what we don't want to do is create like separate silos.
>
> **[6:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/metadata-management?u=76281980&t=365)** We want to build metadata awareness into our AI development culture as well.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **CLI Commands:** make (3)

#### Feature stores
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Feature stores are important because they're a specialized data system that have been specifically designed for managing machine learning features efficiently.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=10)** We use them to serve as a critical bridge between data engineering teams who prepare data and model development teams.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=17)** Now one of the main benefits is that we can centralize features, basically development or computation, as well as the ability to store those features and serve them across different applications within the organization.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=32)** With feature stores, we can ensure consistent feature usage, whether we're in a training environment or a production inference system.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=40)** And also importantly, by implementing feature stores, we can significantly reduce redundancy in our feature development efforts and also ensure reproducibility across different AI workflows.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=54)** There are several core functionalities that are important in feature stores.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=59)** First, they provide a unified storage system that's available across both training and serving environments.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=68)** They also provide for point-in-time correct feature retrieval, which is really essential for accurate model training.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=76)** Also, feature versioning capabilities can ensure that we are able to reproduce models, and comprehensive metadata management includes things like documentation and lineage tracking.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=89)** Also, feature stores can implement access controls and governance features that help us manage permissions for sensitive features.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=97)** The online data store provides low latency feature serving, and that's important, especially during inferencing.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=104)** And in that case, we typically want to use key value stores for low latency feature delivery.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=112)** Now in contrast, we can use offline stores to handle high throughput batch processing, which is useful during training, and we often implement that batch processing using data warehouses.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=126)** Now we also need to have computation pipelines.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=129)** Now feature computation pipelines handle the transformation and other processes that convert raw data into machine learning ready features.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=138)** The feature registry component of feature stores serve as a central repository for feature discovery and documentation.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=146)** And then we also want to include an API layer.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=149)** Now we use the API layer to ensure consistent feature access across different environments from development, notebooks, all the way through to production systems.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=159)** Now let's look at some example use cases where we might develop different features for different business use cases.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=168)** So for example, we might want to have features related to customers.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=171)** Now the features that we can develop can vary from things like customer recency, which tracks the days since the last purchase and helps identify active versus lapsed customers.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=184)** We can also have frequency metrics that calculate the number of purchases in some recent time period, like over the past 90 days.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=192)** A monetary value feature can do things like aggregate spending behavior like calculating the average order value over the past six months.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=201)** We may want to have product affinity scores for customers, and that could give us a measure of a customer's propensity to purchase specific types of products.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=210)** And we may want to have a churn risk score that predicts the probability that a customer might go to a competitor.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=218)** Now if we're talking about products, we're going to have different kinds of features that we might want to keep track of.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=224)** Product popularity features track view-to-purchase conversion rates, and help identify high performing items.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=231)** A seasonality index can capture historical demand variations, but take into account time period, and that could be really useful for inventory planning.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=241)** We might also want to have some metrics around price elasticity, which measures sales response with regards to price changes, and that can help inform optimal pricing strategies.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=254)** Co-purchasing likelihood scores can help indicate the probability or likelihood of products being bought together.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=262)** We can also have stock-out impact features, and those help quantify the historical revenue loss based on inventory gaps.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=270)** And that can help us with things like prioritizing restocking.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=275)** So there's an array of business benefits for using feature stores.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=279)** Organizations typically see significant reduction in feature engineering redundancy, and feature stores help with model development cycles by accelerating the feature reusability across teams and projects.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=295)** Feature stores can also help with governance and compliance because of the centralized feature store and consistent documentation.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=304)** We may see an improvement in data quality through centralized validation and monitoring, and production deployments can become more robust with consistent feature definitions between training and serving.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=318)** When you're implementing feature stores, keep in mind that you want to begin your feature store development by focusing on high value features that are used across multiple models.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=327)** You also want to define clear ownership and governance standards to prevent confusion.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=333)** You want to implement robust monitoring systems to track feature drift and quality metrics.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/feature-stores?u=76281980&t=338)** Be sure to build documentation directly into feature creation workflows, and look to strike the right balance between centralization for efficiency and domain-specific features that you might need across different AI applications.

#### Caching
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] We use caching in AI systems as temporary storage for frequently accessed data or results of computation.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=7)** Now, caching helps reduce latency and computational overheads in our AI pipelines.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=14)** And caching is most effectively used when we place it strategically throughout the AI workflow.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=21)** Now, where we choose to place it depends on kind of a balancing act because we are increasing complexity of our implementation by adding memory usage, but we're gaining on performance here.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=33)** So it's, again, it's a little bit of a trade off, and we use it when the balance favors the performance gains.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=39)** But what we find in most cases is that caching is critical both when we're training models and when we're using models for inference.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=49)** Now, when we implement caching, we're going to use architectures that are quite varied.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=54)** We have essentially a hierarchy that goes from like very low level, small CPU caches all the way up to distributed storage systems.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=62)** So at the low end of the caching sort of scope, we have local and distributed in-memory caching systems, which might be used on a node or a virtual machine.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=72)** We can also have like a higher level abstraction caching where we're caching results of expensive computation, or we're caching features so that we don't have to constantly go back to a feature store, and at highest level, we might cache entire fragments of a model to help with optimizing the loading of that model.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=93)** Now, when we use caching in our data pipelines, there's a few different ways we might want to use caching.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=98)** One is for dataset caching, and here the idea is we want to eliminate repeated iops or IO operations that we're going out and reading from disks or object storage.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=109)** We also use caching when we want to store pre-process features so that we're not constantly applying the same transformations to raw data over and over again.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=120)** Now, another kind of caching that we use isn't so much for having data that's available, say for, you know, a particular feature, but rather caching the entirety of the results of what we've computed so far in our pipeline.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=133)** And we checkpoint those results so that if there is a failure at some point in the future in the pipeline, we can roll back to that checkpoint rather than rolling all the way back and restarting from the beginning of our computations.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=145)** Now, when it comes to inferencing, we, again, have multiple use cases.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=150)** We can use caching for prediction results so that if we're constantly getting requests for a particular set of inputs, well, we know what the prediction is, so we can cache that rather than recalculating each time we get asked about it.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=165)** Caching can also be used for model weights.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=169)** This is especially useful if, for example, using GPUs or other accelerators, and those accelerators have memory that we can use for caching.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=177)** We also use caching when we're working with vectors, and when we're talking about vectors, we're talking about vectors that represent unstructured data, like text in a natural language processing, or an image or audio that gets mapped into a vector representation.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=194)** While it can be very useful to cache those vectors so that, again, we're not constantly going back and reading vectors from their persistent storage location.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=206)** Also with regards to inferences, sometimes there are multiple steps in the inference, and we can store basically those paths or the paths through the computational graph that we use to actually compute those inference paths.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=221)** Now, as we're thinking about caching, we want to start by identifying high impact caching opportunities, and we do that by profiling the performance of our application and the components within that application.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=234)** We also want to remember that, you know, one of the hard problems in computer science is cache invalidation, or knowing when to kind of get rid of your cache with the data you have cached and bring in fresher data, recalculate the data, and store that newer version.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=247)** So we need to experiment oftentimes with cache strategies.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=252)** And we want to be cognizant of the cost caching, especially, you know, really high performance, low latency memory can be expensive.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=261)** So we want to balance memory allocation across different caching layers and use it where it's most effective.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/caching?u=76281980&t=268)** We also want to be sure that we're monitoring our usage, and in particular, we want to look at our hit/miss ratio.

#### Challenge: Feature store capabilities

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> [!info]- Semantic Content

#### Solution: Feature store capabilities
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution-25658622?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution-25658622?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Here's the solution, we use online data stores for low-latency access often during training.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution-25658622?u=76281980&t=11)** Now, we tend to use offline stores when we're working with high-volume batch access scenarios, like during training.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution-25658622?u=76281980&t=20)** Checkpoint caching is used to save partial results, and that allows us to improve resiliency in AI pipelines by allowing us to recover without having to go back to the beginning of a pipeline.

### 7. Real-Time Data Processing for AI Applications

#### Event-driven architectures
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In AI applications, we often use event-driven architectures.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=4)** Now, event-driven architectures are design patterns where systems are created to respond to discrete events as they occur in real time, rather than following some predetermined sequence of actions.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=18)** Now, instead of components directly calling each other components in event-driven architectures communicate through events which create a more flexible mechanism.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=28)** This approach enables loose coupling between services and allows them to scale independently and is needed.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=35)** And it also provides a framework for implementing real-time AI processing capabilities.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=42)** Now, overall, these architectures help us create responsive systems that it can adapt to a range of different conditions that are fairly dynamic.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=53)** Now, if you kind of look under the hood at event-driven architectures, you're going to find some common core components, and these include event producers.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=62)** Now these are components that generate signals when a state change occurs, like an inventory updates or a user does some action on a website.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=71)** There are also event channels.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=73)** These are effectively the transportation layer that move events or the data about events between different components.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=81)** We also have event consumers.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=83)** Now these are services that listen for specific types of events and then react with whatever appropriate processing is required when a particular event occurs.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=94)** Now, event stores are basically data stores.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=97)** They provide persistence, so we have the data stored going into the future, and they also can play a role in terms of replaying capabilities.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=107)** So that allows for like historical reconstruction of an event if we need to maybe troubleshoot or reanalyze a particular sequence of events.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=116)** And we also probably have event schemas.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=118)** These are registries that ensure we have like a consistent interpretation of events across different components.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=126)** Now there are different architecture patterns that can be used with event-driven architectures.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=131)** There's the event notification.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=134)** This is a relatively simple pattern, which just uses events for signaling between components.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=140)** Now a more complicated pattern is the event-carried state transfer pattern.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=145)** Now this is a pattern that includes complete context with each event.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=149)** Now that's useful because that reduces lookups.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=152)** So we have all the information we need when the payload about an event is delivered to a service, rather than say having to go look up in a database.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=161)** Now event sourcing patterns maintain a complete history of all state changes.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=166)** Now this is useful if we want to provide an audit trail and enable for really complex reconstruction patterns.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=174)** Now, event stream processing we've discussed briefly before in terms of stream processing that enables continuous analysis of event flows.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=183)** So that's really useful for things like real-time analytics and monitoring and real-time responding to, for example, adverse events like say, a fraudulent transaction.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=193)** Now let's look at an example of how we might use an event-driven architecture.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=197)** With regards to managing retail inventory.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=201)** Retail inventory systems get updates.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=204)** So for example, a stock level event occurs when products are purchased or restocked.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=211)** Well, an AI demand forecasting model can consume these sort of sales and restocking events to help predict future needs.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=220)** When inventory drops below some critical threshold, we can automatically reorder.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=227)** In addition, we can have dynamic pricing adjustments that occur based on like competitive events, like a price change in another retailer.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=237)** We can also do things like create customer notifications, which are triggered by an item being back in stock when it was previously unavailable.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=246)** There are several benefits to going with event-driven architectures.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=251)** event-driven architectures can improve business responsiveness by enabling immediate reactions to various conditions.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=258)** event-driven architectures also are decoupled by nature, and that kind of decoupled architecture enhances scalability because we can scale different components independently.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=270)** Now, asynchronous processing also allows for greater resilience because the components don't have to wait for each other.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=277)** So for example, we can continue processing in one service while maybe another service might be restarting or rebooting because of an incident or a failure of some type.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=286)** Also, these architectures simplify integration between disparate systems that might otherwise be difficult to connect if they were tightly coupled.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=295)** And one of the nice things about event-driven architectures is if you take advantage of event records and make them immutable, then that's really useful for creating clear audit trails, which can be useful for both compliance and troubleshooting.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=310)** When we're implementing event-driven architectures, we want to begin implementation by defining domain events and the boundaries around those events 'cause we want to make sure we avoid scope creep.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=323)** We also want to implement proper event versioning.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=326)** This helps ensure backward compatibility as the systems and applications evolve.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=332)** We also want to consider the implications of eventual consistency in our databases, which basically means not all data may be immediately updated, so we have to take that into account.
>
> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=344)** We also want to assume that things will fail and that there will be errors.
>
> **[5:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=349)** So we want to ensure that we have, you know, suitable error handling using things like dead letter queues to manage like failed event processing.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/event-driven-architectures?u=76281980&t=357)** And then we also want to have comprehensive monitoring for event flows, and we want to watch for key metrics like throughput and latency because those can help us pretty quickly identify if there are any issues regarding the system health of the, you know, the entire event-driven architecture that we're working with.

#### Real-time data integration patterns
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the design issues we need to think about when we're talking about any kind of real-time data or event-driven architecture is the ability to integrate data in real time.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=11)** Now, real-time data integration enables the continuous synchronization of data across multiple systems, and we can do this with minimal latency.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=21)** Now, this capacity allows AI models to operate on current rather than historical states, so this ability to provide up-to-the-moment insights is really important in a lot of business applications, so for example, it's really critical for time-sensitive decision making.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=37)** Again, fraud is a perfect example where we need to make decisions very quickly.

> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=42)** Now, real-time data integration can also help bridge the traditional gap that we see between operational and analytic data environments, allowing them to work together more effectively.

>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=62)** In real-time data integration, we see a number of different architecture patterns.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=66)** One is called change data captured, commonly referred to just as CDC, and that provides efficient database-level change detection, and we do this by monitoring transaction logs in the database rather than, say, running queries on a regular basis.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=82)** We can also do event-driven integration through message brokers and event streams.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=86)** Now, these are useful when we want to enable loosely coupled systems to communicate.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=91)** We can also use API-based real-time data exchanges using techniques called webhooks and callbacks.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=99)** These provide for immediate notification when some important change happens in a source system.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=105)** Now, the publish and subscribe model is quite common, and we use that when we want to enable scalable data distribution, where producers aren't really concerned about who's consuming their data, but they just want to make sure they make the data available.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=120)** Data virtualization is another architecture pattern, and with data virtualization, we essentially create a unified access layer across disparate source systems without physically moving the data, but this virtual layer that we put on top that provides a unified access point really can help reduce redundancy and complexity.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=141)** Now, within real-time data integration systems, we, again, have multiple components.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=146)** We have stream processing engines, like Apache Flink and Kafka Streams.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=150)** They're useful because they provide the computational framework for the continuous data processing.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=156)** We also have data integration platforms with real-time capabilities, and they often provide connectors that are built and transformation tools that can help expedite the implementation of new data sources being incorporated.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=173)** We also have, sometimes, we use in-memory data grids, and basically, what these do is they allow us to maintain datasets in memory rather than on disc, and those are helpful when we have really high throughput processing requirements.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=187)** API gateways are an important component.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=190)** They essentially provide a standardized data exchange pattern, so they do things like handling things like security processes, like authorizing and authenticating a user, implementing rate limiting, so one consumer doesn't try to overwhelm a system or consume more resources than they really should be consuming at the expense of other users, and then we often use real-time ETL tools.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=217)** These are, you can think of as extensions on the more traditional batch-oriented extract, transformation, and load patterns, where these real-time ETL tools are used for continuous processing, so they enable us to do transformations on the fly as data arrives.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=234)** Now, let's take a look at change data capture, because this is really important when we're working with databases.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=239)** CDC works by capturing database changes at the transaction log level, so that's really an implementation mechanism we use, definitely in relational databases, but other databases as well, and with these transaction logs, we can do things like detect inserts or updates or deletes as they happen in the database, and this approach allows us to propagate modifications from the database with really low latency, like subsecond latency, from a source system to a destination, and it also allows us to do incremental updates, both to the model and the data that we store in those models, and another nice thing about change data capture, or CDC, is that it minimizes the processing overhead, while at the same time, it's actually reducing the latency between the time an update occurs in a database
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=290)** and the time we can reflect that update in some other target system.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=294)** Now, with regards to APIs, this is another commonly used component.
>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=299)** With APIs, we can have synchronous communications through either RESTful or GraphQL interfaces, and these allow for almost immediate request-response patterns, which are important for real-time interactions.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=314)** Now, we can use webhook-based notification mechanisms to push data, and we use that when there's a state change and we want to directly push a change to a subscribing system so that subscribing system can find about the change immediately.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=328)** We can also use streaming APIs for continuous data delivery, so the streaming API is constantly pushing data out to target systems that want to receive that data.
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=340)** Now, APIs can be abused, so it's important to have mechanisms like rate limiting and throttling mechanisms to ensure that we can get predictable performance, and the idea here is we want to prevent any single user or consumer of the API from kind of overwhelming the system.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=358)** Now, another advantage of APIs is that they basically are a standardized interface, and they create consistent integration points, so that's really helpful, especially when we're working with diverse systems that have maybe different underlying technologies.
>
> **[6:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=374)** So let's look at a use case with regards to financial insights.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=378)** Let's imagine that we have, working in a financial services environment, and we have banking transactions that are generating real-time events, and we're using change data capture, CDC, to detect those.
>
> **[6:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=391)** Well, we can integrate that CDC data with other raw transaction data, like data from a merchant or a vendor, and also add context, maybe additional data, say maybe we have zip code, but we might want to add additional data, maybe census data about that zip code, because census features might be useful for model prediction, and then we do something like turn to an AI spending classifier to categorize those transactions, and then those transactions are then further analyzed by a budget analysis engine, and maybe we compare the results of that analysis to historical patterns we know about this particular customer, and based on that, we can personalize notifications that might give insights to the customer,
>
> **[7:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=441)** and we might be able to deliver those within very low latency, within seconds or minutes of the time a particular financial transaction occurred.
>
> **[7:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=451)** So when we're building these kinds of systems, we need to plan for eventual consistency, and here, the idea is that we may have multiple copies of data, like when we have caching or we have redundancy.
>
> **[7:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=463)** We might want to distribute data in multiple places.
>
> **[7:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=467)** Well, it takes time to make sure all the copies are up to date, so in database terminology, what we're dealing with in that case is known as eventual consistency, so we want to keep that in mind anytime we're dealing with very low latency systems, that we might have to deal with eventual consistency.
>
> **[8:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=483)** We also want to implement a robust schema evolution strategy, because data formats are going to change over time, and we want to make sure we have mechanisms for dealing with those changes without breaking our existing systems.
>
> **[8:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=495)** We also want to monitor end-to-end latency across all of our integration points, and that's really important, because we need to be able to identify any bottlenecks that might crop up, and also, we want to make sure we're keeping an eye on performance and make sure we're meeting business requirements and things like SLAs or service-level agreements that we have in place.
>
> **[8:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/real-time-data-integration-patterns?u=76281980&t=515)** And finally, we want to make sure we're balancing the real-time needs that we have from a business perspective against the complexity and cost of maintaining this infrastructure that's able to kind of keep these low-latency real-time processing pipelines operating and operating reliably.

#### Monitoring and alerting systems
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980)
