> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Monitoring systems provide continuous observation of our AI system's behavior, performance, and health.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=8)** Now these capabilities are critical for maintaining reliability in real time AI processing environments where a failure can have immediate impact.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=18)** Now, effective monitoring is going to span multiple layers, from the infrastructure components that implement the hardware, to data pipelines that move the data to model performance metrics.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=29)** But by implementing proper monitoring, we can enable issue detection so that we can address problems before users experience any negative impact.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=39)** Now, this visibility also forms a foundation for automated remediation and continuous optimization in our systems.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=47)** There are several areas we want to take into account when we're monitoring.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=51)** Infrastructure metrics capture the fundamental health of our computing resources, and these include resources like CPU, memory, network, and storage.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=61)** With regards to data pipelines, the health monitoring there focuses on operational metrics, like throughput rates, processing latency, and back pressure indicators that might signal we have a bottleneck somewhere in the downstream.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=75)** Now, model performance monitoring tracks things, like accuracy metrics, indicators of drift in our data, and prediction latency.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=83)** And that helps to ensure our AI components are, actually, functioning as expected.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=89)** Now of course, at the end of the day, we have to tie all of this back to business.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=94)** So we want to have business KPI monitoring that connects the technical performance to some actual business outcome, like tracking conversion rates or user engagement patterns.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=105)** We also, of course, want to monitor for security and compliance reasons.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=109)** Now security monitoring examines access patterns and data handling procedures to help ensure, the system is meeting our regulatory requirements.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=119)** Now we have several different components in monitoring systems.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=123)** We often use distributed tracing technology to provide end-to-end visibility, and to request flows.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=130)** We have structured logging, which provides contact rich information, time series metrics collection, and that's important for enabling both realtime dashboards and historical trend analysis.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=142)** We may use correlation engines across these different metrics and logs to help connect seemingly unrelated events.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=149)** And then finally, we may want to employ centralized observability platforms that combine elements into unified dashboards and provides a comprehensive view across your AI infrastructure.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=162)** Now with AI monitoring, or AI specific monitoring, we want to look at things, like feature distribution monitoring, which tracks statistical properties of model inputs and helps us detect concept drift.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=175)** We also want to pay attention to prediction accuracy, like tracking model outputs, and comparing those against ground truth to ensure that we're getting the performance that we expect.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=186)** Now, model latency profiling is important 'cause that helps us understand how different inputs might affect performance, and that can help us identify performance bottlenecks and optimize inference times.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=200)** Now, alerting is another aspect related to monitoring.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=203)** Alerting can include multi-level severity classification.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=208)** Now, these categorizations are based on business impact, and we use them to ensure that we have an appropriate response to particular levels of alerts.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=220)** Now, threshold based alert triggers notify us when key metrics exceed some predefined boundaries, and that might indicate a potential problem.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=229)** Now, anomaly detection is another kind of alerting, and that helps us identify unexpected behavioral patterns and that might trigger threshold alerts, but it might not, but it still represents some kind of abnormal state in the system that warrants investigation.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=246)** We may employ composite alerts that combine multiple signals.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=250)** Now we do this often to reduce noise and prevent alert fatigue, which can occur when we have alerts that are triggered on a single threshold.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=260)** And then we may also use what's known as progressive notification escalation.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=264)** This ensures that issues receive appropriate attention.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=268)** Now, when we're alerted to something, there's probably something that needs attention and needs to be fixed.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=273)** That's where remediation comes in.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=276)** Self-healing capabilities enable systems to automatically recover from common failure scenarios without requiring human interaction.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=284)** Now, we can also use things, like automatic scaling mechanisms, to adjust resources based on load prediction patterns.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=291)** That'll help us maintain performance during spikes in demand.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=295)** We may also want to employ fallback mechanisms.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=298)** For example, we might want to use simpler models to ensure that we can continue to deliver service, even during a disruption.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=305)** For example, if we no longer have the resources to run maybe compute intensive models, we can run a simpler model, which can provide basic functionality.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=315)** We may also want to employ circuit breakers.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=318)** Now these are mechanisms that prevent cascading failures by isolating problematic components before they can have adverse effects on other components in the system.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=328)** And then also, we can employ shadow deployments.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=332)** This is for comparing rollouts.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=334)** So for example, we can do safe rollouts by comparing new versions in a shadow deployment environment and then comparing how that shadow deployment is behaving compared to the current production system.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=347)** And we can analyze any differences and make sure we understand why they might occur before we roll out that new deployment into our production environment.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=356)** Now when we're implementing monitoring and alerting, we want to begin the implementation by focusing on critical path monitoring before expanding coverage to less critical components.
>
> **[6:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=366)** We want to make sure that we have clear, service level objectives, or SLOs, for each component, 'cause that allows us to define what a healthy state of that system actually looks like.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=376)** We want to implement proper tagging and metadata 'cause that'll provide important contextual information that we'll use with alerts.
>
> **[6:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=385)** We also want to design dashboards for different stakeholders because each different kind of stakeholders is going to bring a different perspective.
>
> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=393)** Like we'll have technical operators who are going to want to, maybe, understand infrastructure monitoring versus business leaders who might be more interested in business KPIs.
>
> **[6:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/monitoring-and-alerting-systems?u=76281980&t=402)** And then also ,it's just in general a good practice to conduct regular incident reviews, 'cause that'll help us improve our monitoring effectiveness, based on real world experiences.

### 8. Secure Data Management for AI Implementation

#### Security compliance and regulation
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Regulatory frameworks around AI are evolving rapidly.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=4)** And we're seeing evolution both from governments and industry organizations that are trying to address risks that are specific to AI systems.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=13)** And what we're finding is that security requirements for these AI services typically span three areas: Protecting training and influencing data, ensuring our model integrity, and then also maintaining algorithmic fairness.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=28)** We see compliance obligations that can vary dramatically depending on the industry that we're in, but also the geographic region that we're in.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=37)** So, that's really driving organizations to carefully balance, you know, how quickly they are moving in terms of their own innovation regarding AI, with regards to ensuring that they are constantly in compliance, 'cause obviously we want to avoid penalties or any kind of reputational damage that can occur if we're not in compliance.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=58)** And what we may find is that organizations that become good at this balance of innovation and adhering to regulations, will actually realize a competitive advantage in the marketplace, because they'll be able to build additional trust with customers and business partners.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=75)** Now, there are several key regulatory frameworks that are worth being aware of.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=79)** Even if they don't specifically apply to you or your organization, they may have regulations or requirements that may be something that will eventually apply to your domain.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=91)** So for example, the GDPR, or General Data Protection Regulation in the EU, establish many of the principles that we now see in AI regulations, including things like data minimization, and purpose limitations.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=106)** There's also HIPAA, which creates specific requirements for handling protected healthcare information in the US.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=112)** And the Fair Credit Reporting Act, or FCRA, is especially relevant for organizations that are developing AI services that will be used in things like consumer lending or consumer credit assessments.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=127)** And then there's also, the state of California in the US has created a couple of acts, the Consumer Privacy Act, and the Privacy Rights Acts, which have established some of the most comprehensive data rights in the US.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=138)** And even though the legislation strictly applies only to California, just given their market size, it tends to have a ripple effect through how businesses implement regulations for all of their customers in the US.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=153)** And then there are also industry-specific regulations.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=156)** And this is especially the case if you're in a highly regulated industry like healthcare or financial services.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=163)** Now, what we see across all of these different compliance frameworks are some common requirements.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=170)** One of them is transparency in AI decision-making.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=174)** And we often hear about this in terms of regulations that require explainability for decisions.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=181)** Data minimization is another requirement, and that, basically the principle that requires us to only collect what's necessary for our specific use cases.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=190)** And consent management has really evolved beyond sort of the idea of, oh, I just need to display, you know, some long detailed legalese, and have somebody check a box.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=200)** Now what we're finding is consent management is getting much more granular with regards to data collection and data processing.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=207)** And then there are also documentation requirements.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=210)** So now we have to, for example, be able to document our entire remodel lifecycle, from development through validation, and on through to deployment.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=221)** And we may also need to do regular security assessments.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=224)** So, basically, do things like scan for vulnerabilities, and check for algorithmic fairness.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=230)** And then it's becoming more important that we have comprehensive audit trails, because these allow us to basically track all of the system activities.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=238)** And then if we need to, we can demonstrate that we are in compliance because we have the audit logs to demonstrate that.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=246)** Now, when we think about security and how we implement security, we often talk about security controls.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=251)** And there are some that are just common to information security in general, like identity and access management systems, which from an AI perspective, are important for controlling who can access models and data.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=265)** There's also the need for end-to-end encryption.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=268)** So, that protects data while it's in transit, like in a pipeline, as well as when it's at rest, for example, in storage.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=275)** And then there are also really AI-specific security controls, like the need for specialized protections against adversarial attacks on the models themselves.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=286)** Because without them, you know, the model outputs could be manipulated, or an attacker might be able to extract training data from our model.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=295)** We sometimes use differential privacy implementations, which is basically a mathematical technique for adding noise.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=302)** And that's useful if we want to prevent individual data points from being identified.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=308)** And then also, we have to think in terms of implementation and DevOps.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=312)** We want to make sure we secure our deployment pipelines.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=315)** So we want to have, you know, integrity validations steps to ensure our models haven't been tampered with.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=323)** Now, when it comes to implementing a compliance program, one of the first things we need to do, is basically start by designating clear ownership of AI compliance.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=332)** Now, this often entails cross-functional teams with both technical and legal expertise.
>
> **[5:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=341)** We also want to be able to conduct comprehensive risk assessments, because we want to look at for both general and AI-specific vulnerabilities in the system.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=350)** And this goes back, again, to like, the different types of security controls that we would use.
>
> **[5:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=355)** We also want to establish model governance frameworks for things that standardized development, validation, and deployment.
>
> **[6:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=362)** And we want to make sure that we have common frameworks or common practices that we can use across our organization.
>
> **[6:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=371)** We also want to implement data provenance tracking and model versioning, that'll help maintain lineage of our models.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=378)** And we want to make sure we have standard documentation.
>
> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=381)** So think in terms of templates, especially those that, you know, might be required for specific regulatory requirements.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/security-compliance-and-regulation?u=76281980&t=388)** And then finally think about designing regular testing protocols to assess how compliant we are on an ongoing basis, rather than wait for say, you know, annual audits or one-time project checks.

#### Privacy-preserving AI methods
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Working on AI systems brings with it an array of privacy challenges.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=4)** Now, traditional AI models often require direct access to sensitive data, and this creates a tension between the need for data for analysis and the need to protect privacy.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=16)** Now, some regulations like GDPR and CCPA impose strict requirements on how organizations can collect, process, and use personal data.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=25)** And this creates what's known as the privacy-utility trade-off.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=29)** It's basically the challenge of maintaining model performance while limiting our access to raw data.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=35)** Now, fortunately, there are a number of privacy preserving methods that we can use to enable us to do continued development in AI while still protecting sensitive information.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=49)** One of those techniques is known as federated learning.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=52)** Now, federated learning is really a paradigm shift in how we train AI models, because rather than doing centralized training, we distribute the process across multiple devices without centralizing raw data.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=66)** So instead of collecting all the data in one location, we only send model updates while the original data remains secure in its local home location.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=79)** This enables collaboration between organizations that couldn't otherwise share data, maybe due to competitive concerns or other regulations.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=88)** And another thing about federated learning is that it reduces regulatory risk while still maintaining relatively comparable model performance to what we would expect from traditional training approaches.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=100)** Now, another type of control is differential privacy.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=106)** Differential privacy is a mathematical framework which works with formal privacy guarantees.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=111)** So it's not just a technique that works most of the time, but it's actually a rigorous approach, you know, that has theorems and provable properties behind it.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=121)** Now it works by adding calibrated statistical noise to data or to model outputs.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=127)** And basically what that does is it masks the contribution of any single individual.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=132)** One of the things that's so powerful about differential privacy is that it enables a quantifiable privacy-utility trade-off measure.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=142)** And it has this concept called a privacy budget.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=145)** And basically that allows organizations to, in a very quantifiable way, manage their disclosure risks.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=154)** So organizations can implement differential privacy at various stages.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=158)** We can do it during data collection, through the model training or at the inference stage.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=164)** A third mechanism or technique is called homomorphic encryption.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=169)** Now, homomorphic encryption is a cryptographic approach that is privacy preserving, because basically what it does, it enables us to do computations, like aggregating data or analyzing data in different ways, without decrypting the data.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=187)** Now, this provides cryptographic guarantees that sensitive information remains protected throughout the entire processing pipeline.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=195)** And this is especially suitable or valuable for high compliance industries like healthcare and finance.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=203)** And we see it in use in real world applications that include things like secure auctions where, for example, we want bids to remain encrypted or in private medical research on sensitive patient data or in financial services, for example, where we might want to preserve privacy around fraud detection, especially if we're working across multiple organizations.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=225)** Now, when it comes to privacy-preserving AI techniques, we want to make sure we start by aligning the methods with our specific privacy requirements, and we want to ensure that our technical approach is in line with whatever regulatory frameworks apply to us.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=242)** We want to make sure we implement comprehensive privacy governance frameworks, and those have to include things like policies, procedures, and architectural standards.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=252)** We also want to balance privacy enhancement against model performance requirements.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=257)** Typically, what we find is more privacy means some performance trade off.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=262)** And it's a good practice to consider hybrid approaches that combine multiple privacy-preserving techniques.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=268)** And this provides a layered protection, kind of like what we see in traditional cybersecurity with the principle of defense in depth, in which case we don't depend on a single security control to protect us.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=281)** We have multiple controls.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=282)** So if one fails, the others will still be available to protect us.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/privacy-preserving-ai-methods?u=76281980&t=285)** This is a similar idea when we're using hybrid approaches and privacy-preserving techniques.

#### Data governance frameworks
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-governance-frameworks?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-governance-frameworks?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Data governance represents a structured framework for treating data as a strategic asset rather than just some byproduct of business operations.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-governance-frameworks?u=76281980&t=9)** At its core, governance defines clear roles and responsibilities for, one, who makes decisions about data.

>

>

> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/data-governance-frameworks?u=76281980&t=348)** And also we just want to recognize that governance is an ongoing process rather than a one-time initiative.

#### Audit trails and logging
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] AI audit trails can create comprehensive records of all the system interactions and decisions throughout the AI ecosystem.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=9)** Now, we can use these to track who accesses data, when changes occur, and what specific actions users take within the system.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=19)** Now, effective audit trails essentially document every phase of the model lifecycle, from training and validation through deployment and through to inference operations.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=29)** Now, these records are important because they provide critical evidence that are important for regulatory compliance, and also they can support our own internal security incident investigations.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=42)** Now we have logging requirements associated with auditing.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=45)** We want to track all model lifecycle events from dataset creation through training, testing, deployment, and decommissioning.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=54)** We also want to track every instance when someone accesses, modifies, deletes, or exports data across the environment.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=62)** We should also be recording all authentication activities, things like login attempts, permission changes, as well as privilege escalations.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=71)** Ideally, we're also capturing inference requests and responses, and we want to include rich contextual metadata 'cause that helps establish the complete decision context.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=81)** We should also log all system configuration changes, particularly security related modifications that could affect system integrity.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=90)** And also we want to make sure we establish an unbroken data lineage from system source through transformation to the final model outputs.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=99)** When it comes to the technical implementation, we want to make sure we implement an immutable, tamper-proof logging system, and we want to employ cryptographic techniques to prevent unauthorized modifications.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=111)** We also want to aggregate logs from distributed systems into a centralized repository that'll give us comprehensive visibility.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=119)** We also want to structure our log formats with consistent schemas, that can really improve search capabilities and help us enable automated analysis.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=129)** We should be deploying continuous monitoring systems to scan logs for suspicious patterns and trigger alerts for us on potential security incidents.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=139)** We also want to protect audit information itself with strict role-based access controls.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=144)** And here we want to follow the best practice in cybersecurity, which is known as least privilege.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=151)** So only those who need access to do their jobs should be given access.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=157)** Now, there are multiple ways we can use audit trails and logs.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=161)** We can use them for generating evidence for regulatory examinations to demonstrate that we are in compliance with the industry or government regulations.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=170)** There are also useful for security in incident investigations.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=174)** These logs can help us establish attack timelines, identify affected systems, and determine what data was exposed.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=182)** They can also be used by those who are working on model fairness and assessing performance, for example, to detect drift.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=191)** We can also identify disparate impact across different demographic groups using the details that are available to us in audit trails and logs.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=200)** These are also important for validating privacy control effectiveness.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=203)** They're essentially documenting the proper implementation of data minimization and consent processes.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=210)** They're also useful for conducting root cause analysis.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=213)** They'll allow us to trace the complete event chain leading to say, for example, an anomalous prediction or some kind of system failure.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=222)** Another thing that's useful about audit trails is when we're actually correcting a problem.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=227)** They can document the remediation actions to prove that we've essentially done what we should do to address whatever issue was identified.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/audit-trails-and-logging?u=76281980&t=236)** And it also creates accountability to all of the stakeholders that we are in fact addressing issues as they arise.

#### Challenge: Privacy-preserving methods
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/challenge-25658623?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/challenge-25658623?u=76281980&t=0)** (bright upbeat music)
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/challenge-25658623?u=76281980&t=5)** - [Instructor] Okay, for this challenge, I'd like you to identify what type of privacy preserving method allows us to process encrypted data without first decrypting it.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/challenge-25658623?u=76281980&t=15)** And then secondly, I'd like you to identify the type of privacy preserving method that allows us to avoid centralizing raw training data in a single location.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)
> **Non-Speech:** (bright upbeat music) (1)

#### Solution: Privacy-preserving methods
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution?u=76281980&t=0)** (bright music)
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution?u=76281980&t=5)** - [Instructor] Okay, the solution or the answer to the first question is homomorphic encryption.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution?u=76281980&t=9)** That's the type of encryption that allows us to process data without first decrypting it.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution?u=76281980&t=15)** And then secondly, federated learning is a technique which allows us to leave raw training data distributed across multiple platforms or servers, rather than centralizing all of that data into a single location.

### 9. Ethical Considerations

#### AI ethics and responsible data use
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=6)** Now, as we're developing AI, we have to actively balance our desire to advance the technology with the need to minimize societal risks.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=16)** So, for example, we want to watch for and address the potential harms that can come from biased algorithmic decision making.

>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=67)** We also want accountability.
>

>

>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=98)** Now, one place we can start is with ethical data collection.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=102)** Here we want to be sure we secure informed consent by clearly articulating what data we're collecting, how we'll use it, and who will access it.

>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=123)** We also want to implement straightforward mechanisms for consent withdrawal and data deletion.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=129)** And we want to apply data minimalization principles.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=133)** And we do this by collecting only what's necessary for specific legitimate purposes.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=138)** And we want to regularly perform audits to identify and remediate bias in the data sets.
>

>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ai-ethics-and-responsible-data-use?u=76281980&t=159)** Also, we want to assign specific accountability for ethical oversight at both team and executive levels.

>

>

#### Transparency and explainability
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Transparency enables us to identify and fix bias, errors, and vulnerabilities throughout the AI development lifecycle.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=9)** Regulatory frameworks now mandate explainability.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=13)** So for example, GDPR requires meaningful information about automated decisions, and the EU AI Act establishes tiered transparency requirements.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=25)** Modern AI's technical complexity creates real barriers to understanding.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=30)** For example, with large neural networks containing billions of parameters, they don't really lend themselves to intuitive interpretation.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=38)** And these lead to opaque models that generate accountability gaps that undermine trust in the AI ecosystem.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=46)** There are multiple dimensions of transparency.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=49)** Data transparency reveals what feeds our models, including sources, pre-processing steps, and potential biases.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=58)** Now, algorithmic transparency deals with how we explain how our models function internally, and it involves showing the mathematical process that converts the inputs to the outputs.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=70)** Operational transparency documents how we deploy and maintain AI systems in production environments, including how we monitor and update our procedures.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=82)** Outcome transparency is a type of transparency that deals with the impact and performance metrics of AI decisions.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=90)** And then finally, governance transparency talks about roles, responsibilities, and oversight mechanisms that we use to guide our AI development and deployment.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=101)** Now, when we talk about explanations, there are different types of explanations we can build.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=106)** We can use, for example, feature important techniques.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=110)** They quantify which inputs most significantly includes a models outputs.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=116)** This helps to highlight the key factors that drive predictions or decisions.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=121)** We can also use example based explanations to identify which training examples most shaped a particular outcome.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=130)** Now, with contrastive explanations, we clarify why the system chose one option over another.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=135)** And we do this by addressing the question, "Why not X instead?"
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=140)** Or some other value instead of the decision that was made.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=144)** Now, counterfactual explanations specify what change would produce a different result.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=151)** Now this is useful, 'cause it can give stakeholders insights into how they can achieve certain outcomes.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=157)** And then also it's important to share confidence metrics.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=162)** Those communicate the system certainty level about predictions, and that can help users gauge reliability across different scenarios.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=170)** We have different ways of implementing transparency and explanations.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=175)** We can use post hoc explanation tools like LIME and SHAP, which create interpretable approximations of complex models.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=184)** These are useful for generating insights without adversely affecting performance.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=190)** Now, inherently interpretable models, such as decision trees, offer transparency by design.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=196)** So making their decision logic directly observable and auditable is highly useful in this case.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=203)** Attention mechanism used by some algorithms highlight which specific input features affect predictions most strongly, and they can show where the model focuses during processing.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=214)** Now, counterfactual explanations, again, those show users how different input changes would affect outcomes.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=221)** And so that, in some ways, it provides a practical path for seeing different kinds of results.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=228)** Now, sometimes we want our explanations centered not so much around implementation, but around our stakeholders.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=237)** So for example, technical teams require detailed model mechanics information so that they can debug, optimize, and address edge cases during development.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=246)** Now, business users, on the other hand, need business-oriented insights.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=251)** Those are things that connect technical details to operational impact.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=255)** And end users, on the other hand, typically demand clear rationales for decisions that affect them personally.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=262)** So in that case, we want to focus on pragmatic information rather than technical details.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=267)** And then if you're dealing with regulators, we could imagine that they would like to seek evidence demonstrating compliance with legal requirements and fairness across different demographic groups.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=278)** So how do we deal with this from an implementation perspective?
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=282)** Well, we want to incorporate explainability requirements during initial system design phases.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=288)** It's much easier to start with that in mind rather than trying to retrofit transparency later on.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=295)** We also want to choose modeling approaches and frameworks based on our transparency needs.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=302)** We should build or develop tailored explanation interfaces for different stakeholder groups.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=306)** And accordingly, we'll customize the detail level and terminology based on those groups.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=313)** We should also have a way to methodically test explanation quality.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=318)** And we ideally, we could do this with actual users to verify that they can comprehend the explanation, and the explanation makes sense to people with varying technical expertise levels.
>
> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=330)** We also want to document our explanation methodologies, and importantly, we want to include in that documentation the limitations of those methods.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=339)** And finally, we want to implement feedback mechanisms.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/transparency-and-explainability?u=76281980&t=342)** And this is going to help us continuously improve explanation quality based on the feedback we receive from users.

#### Ethical guidelines and standards
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now let's look at some specific ethical frameworks.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=4)** The IEEE Global Initiative provides a comprehensive standard for ethical AI.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=9)** Now, it focuses specifically on autonomous systems and establishing technical guidelines for engineers and developers.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=16)** The OECD AI Principles is a consensus framework document endorsed by 42 different countries, and it emphasizes human-centered approaches to trustworthy AI development.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=28)** The European Commission's guidelines for trustworthy AI establishes requirements for AI systems operating within the EU.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=37)** UNESCO's Recommendations on ethical AI is a global framework adopted by 193 different countries, and it addresses ethical implications of AI with special attention to developing nations.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=50)** And then industry has also developed a series of frameworks.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=55)** Leading technology companies each have their own framework.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=58)** With Microsoft emphasizing responsible AI through transparent documentation, Google's framework focuses on societal benefit and IBM's prioritizes fairness, and explicability in their approach.

> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=70)** Now, when it comes to ethics in operations, there are several things we want to keep in mind.

>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/ethical-guidelines-and-standards?u=76281980&t=86)** This will help us identify any potential harm to individuals or communities.
>

>

#### Solution: Ethical principles
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution-25655727?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution-25655727?u=76281980&t=0)** (bright electronic music)
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-planning-strategy-and-compliance-for-ai-initiatives/solution-25655727?u=76281980&t=5)** - [Instructor] Okay, the solution entails the answer to the first question, which is, the principle of fairness calls for preventing and mitigating bias in training data and decision-making, while the principle of transparency calls for enabling users and other stakeholders to understand how AI systems function and how they make decisions.
